### RV-0128 · FE-PUB-10 · Canonical Vendor Subdomain (URL builder + microsite metadata) · Team-1
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Pages in scope: owns no pages (touches P-PUB-13..17 vendor microsite + every public surface linking out to a vendor profile) · Reviewed SHA: `cafefcb` (checkpoint; `954e430` is a trivial 1-line WP-card SHA-fill, not re-reviewed separately) · Lane G — realizes ADR-024 / `governanceReviews/BOARD-PACKET-CANONICAL-VENDOR-SUBDOMAIN_v1.0.md` in presentation-mode interim (Board ruling ratified `c1187a8`, agenda #12).
- Scope: new `app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts` (`vendorHref(slug, subpage?)`, the single canonical URL builder — ADR-024 Vendor URL Builder rule, SHALL); 16 files repointed off inline `` `/vendors/${slug}` `` concatenation; `alternates.canonical` + `openGraph.url` added to all 7 vendor-microsite route `generateMetadata` functions. Acceptance criterion (Board agenda #12 / WP card): "pixel output of all existing pages identical — only URL generation, routing, metadata, redirects, discovery artifacts may change."
- **Review-A verdict: PASS — BLOCKER=0 · MAJOR=0 · MINOR=0** (+ 2 OBS, non-gating). Confirmed: the narrow presentation-mode-interim scoping is a faithful, non-overreaching realization of the packet's item 6 (canonical/og:url) and item 10 (CHR Invariant / URL Builder rule, SHALL — quoted byte-accurately); `vendorHref` output byte-identical to every pre-commit inline pattern (diffed against `cafefcb~1`); zero remaining hardcoded call sites repo-wide via grep; both legacy redirect stubs (`capabilities`→`about`, `certifications`→`resources`) unchanged targets, only construction mechanism changed; all 7 routes' canonical/og:url spot-checked correct, no cross-route copy-paste contamination; out-of-scope boundaries held (no middleware/sitemap/robots/redirect-matrix code; cross-track buyer file `discover-view.tsx:60` confirmed genuinely untouched); no governance-signal/firewall surface touched; the disclosed pre-existing `landmark-unique` a11y finding (duplicate `"Vendor sections"` nav label) independently confirmed via `git diff` as unrelated to this commit (href-value only, zero DOM/aria change) — correctly disclosed, not silently dropped, not fixed (out of pixel-identical scope). Live-rendered `/vendors`, microsite home, `about` — correct. OBS-1: the Board packet itself has a pre-existing internal label collision ("Decision 6" vs. numbered item 10) for the same rule — a packet-authoring defect, not attributable to this milestone. OBS-2: one intermittent, unrelated, uncommitted-buyer-track `tsc` error traced to a different in-progress track's WIP file, confirmed unrelated.
- **Review-B verdict: ISSUES** — 1 MINOR + 2 OBS, empirical/adversarial pass (isolated-worktree production build attempt — blocked by a pre-existing, commit-independent Windows EPERM tracer defect reproduced identically on `cafefcb~1`, confirmed not a regression, fell back to `next dev` per this program's documented workaround; real Playwright verification of both redirects via `page.url()` post-navigation, not curl; confirmed `alternates.canonical`/`openGraph.url` resolve to genuinely **absolute** URLs via `metadataBase`; adversarial slug-injection probe against `getPublicVendorProfile`'s fixed-seed lookup — no pass-through, no crash; broader hardcode sweep beyond Review-A's grep pattern — zero additional hits; fresh axe-core sweep — only the one already-disclosed pre-existing violation, no new ones; text-content + screenshot-hash diff on 3 routes — byte-identical before/after, sole PNG delta was the Next dev-mode overlay badge, not app content).
  - **MINOR** (`app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts`): Review-B's isolated-worktree `npx prettier --check` reportedly failed on the `VendorSubpage` union-type formatting, contradicting the commit message's "tsc/eslint/prettier green" claim.
  - OBS-2/OBS-3 (env/methodology, non-actionable against this milestone): the same pre-existing EPERM `next build` blocker independently rediscovered; one false-negative in Review-B's own Playwright harness (cold dev-route compile race) self-corrected by repeat runs within the same review.
- **Disposition (author/authority, Validate Findings gate, CLAUDE.md §13) — MINOR finding investigated, does NOT reproduce against the authoritative repo state:**
  1. **Valid?** — Empirically NO, against the actual committed content. `git status`/`git diff` confirm zero working-tree drift from `cafefcb` on this file. `npx prettier --check` on the working file: **passes** ("uses Prettier code style"). `npx prettier --write`: reports **"unchanged."** Direct `diff` of prettier's own reformatted output against the committed file: **empty (byte-identical)**. Re-ran `git show cafefcb:"app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts" | npx prettier --check --stdin-filepath ...` directly against the git blob (bypassing the working tree entirely): **passes**. Four independent methods, one answer: this file conforms to this repo's pinned prettier config (`.prettierrc`: `printWidth:100` — the union type's single-line form is 103 chars, over budget, so prettier's own preferred formatting **is** the committed 6-line wrap; this is not a violation, it's what prettier itself produces).
  2. **Likely root cause of the discrepancy (recorded, not asserted as fact):** Review-B's isolated worktree used a fresh `pnpm install --no-frozen-lockfile` (per this program's own documented worktree-build pattern, needed to avoid Turbopack's symlink rejection) against `package.json`'s caret range `"prettier": "^3.4.2"` — a different resolved patch/minor version than this repo's installed `3.8.5` could plausibly format long union types differently. Not independently confirmed (would require inspecting that worktree's `node_modules/prettier/package.json`, which no longer exists), so recorded as the leading hypothesis, not a ruling.
  3. **Per `review-process.md` §13, Validate-Findings disposition on a raised finding is owner/Board-reserved, not unilaterally decided by the owning Dev team** — this entry does NOT self-rule the finding invalid. Instead: no code change was made (there is nothing to fix — the committed file already matches prettier's own output byte-for-byte), and a **fresh, independent Review-A** is being dispatched per Amendment v1.3's literal "any Review-B ISSUES → re-enter at Review-A" rule, briefed with this full dispute record, to independently re-run `prettier --check` against the actual `cafefcb` commit (not a fresh worktree reinstall) and rule on it. This mirrors the RV-0125 precedent (a disputed Review-B finding resolved by independent-reviewer convergence, not unilateral dismissal).
- Board: pending (routes through the re-entered Review-A cycle below; not a BLOCKER/REGRESSION, no Flag-and-Halt triggered — a disputed MINOR under active re-verification). Result: 🟠 Revising (procedural — zero code delta) → re-entering Review-A. Continued below.

- **Re-entered Review-A (independent, fresh context) — verdict: PASS. Disputed MINOR does NOT hold; original PASS stands; dispute fully resolved.**
  - Scope of this re-entry per Amendment v1.3: adjudicate only the one disputed MINOR (prettier formatting of `VendorSubpage` union type); no code changed since `cafefcb`, no re-review of the full original scope.
  - Independently reproduced, from scratch, without deferring to either side's prior claim:
    1. **Drift check**: `git status --porcelain -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → empty. `git diff -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → empty. Working tree exactly matches `cafefcb` for this file.
    2. **Config**: `.prettierrc` at repo root → `{"printWidth": 100, "trailingComma": "all"}`.
    3. **`npx prettier --check` on the working file** (main repo, not an isolated worktree) → `"All matched files use Prettier code style!"` — passes.
    4. **Byte-exact blob test**: `git show cafefcb:"app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` piped through `npx prettier --stdin-filepath "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"`, output diffed against the committed blob directly (not the working-tree copy) → `diff` exit code 0, zero output. Byte-identical. This bypasses the working tree entirely and tests the actual committed git object.
    5. **Version cross-check**: `npx prettier --version` in this repo → `3.9.1`. `package.json` pins `"prettier": "^3.4.2"`. `pnpm-lock.yaml` resolves `prettier@3.9.1` for that specifier. So this repo's installed prettier (`3.9.1`) and the lockfile-pinned resolution (`3.9.1`) are the **same exact version** — no ambiguity, no range to second-guess. (Note: this repo's `node_modules` and the lockfile agree on `3.9.1`; Team-1's dispute record cited a locally-observed `3.8.5` from an earlier check — either way, both `3.8.5` and `3.9.1` produce the identical wrapped output confirmed here, so the discrepancy is not attributable to version drift on this repo's side.)
    6. **printWidth sanity check**: single-line form `export type VendorSubpage = "about" | "products" | "projects" | "industries" | "contact" | "resources";` measured at **103 characters** — over the configured `printWidth: 100`. Prettier's own line-length rule mandates a wrap here; the committed 6-line vertical-bar form is the *only* conformant output, not a stylistic choice. A single-line rendering would itself be the violation.
  - **Conclusion**: the committed file at `cafefcb` does **not** violate this repo's prettier formatting rules. Four independent verification methods (working-tree check, stdin/blob check, manual width count against the pinned config, and version-identity confirmation) converge on one answer: no. Review-B's isolated-worktree finding does not reproduce against this repo's actual toolchain or the actual committed git object, under any measurement. The commit message's "tsc/eslint/prettier green" claim is accurate.
  - **Drift sanity pass**: `git log --oneline -5 -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → single commit (`cafefcb`) touches this file, no follow-ups. `git status --porcelain` shows only unrelated files dirty (other in-flight governance/milestone work: `esc_registry.md`, `changelog.md`, `execution-board.md`, this review log, and untracked docs for an unrelated buyer/vendor-directory package) — nothing under any `cafefcb`-touched path (per `git show cafefcb --stat`, 18 files) is dirty. No regression, no drift since the original Review-A PASS.
  - **Verdict: PASS — BLOCKER=0 · MAJOR=0 · MINOR=0.** The disputed MINOR is adjudicated invalid (fails Validate-Findings gate step 1, "Valid?" — not factually correct against the committed artifact). Original Review-A PASS (line 1679) stands unmodified; this re-entry ratifies it independently rather than overriding it. Gate clears. Milestone may proceed to a fresh Review-B re-check per the normal pipeline, or the Board may treat this dispute as closed given two independent, convergent, fully-reproducible empirical rulings (Team-1's investigation + this independent re-entry) against one non-reproducing isolated-environment claim.
  - Leading hypothesis for Review-B's original observation (still unconfirmed, recorded for completeness, not load-bearing to this verdict): an isolated-worktree `pnpm install --no-frozen-lockfile` could in principle resolve a different prettier patch version than this repo's pinned lockfile — but this is moot here, since this repo's own installed version (`3.9.1`) is confirmed lockfile-exact and still produces the committed formatting, i.e. there is no prettier version reachable via the `^3.4.2` range that would need Review-B's claimed single-line collapse when `printWidth:100` and a 103-char candidate line are both fixed facts.

- **Re-check Review-B (independent, fresh context, tie-breaker per owner dispatch) — verdict: PASS. Gate confirmed clear on `cafefcb`; milestone ready for Dev-team self-close.**
  - Scope of this re-check per Amendment v1.3 (`review-process.md` §13): confirm A:PASS ∧ B:PASS land on the same checkpoint SHA before close. Not a full from-scratch adversarial pass — the first Review-B's empirical work (isolated-build attempt, Playwright redirect verification, slug-injection probe, hardcode sweep, axe sweep, pixel-diff) was thorough and its non-prettier findings stand as clean without re-doing them; this pass is a third-opinion tie-break on the one disputed MINOR plus a drift/regression sanity check.
  - **Drift/regression check**: `git show cafefcb --stat` → 18 files, exact match to the record in this entry. `git status --porcelain -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → empty; `git diff -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → empty. `git log --oneline -5 -- "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` → single commit (`cafefcb`), no follow-ups. Broader repo `git status --porcelain` shows dirty/untracked files, but all are unrelated in-flight work (`esc_registry.md`, `changelog.md`, `execution-board.md`, this review log, an untracked buyer/vendor-directory governance package) — nothing under any of the 18 `cafefcb`-touched paths is dirty. HEAD has moved on to later unrelated milestones (`FE-DOC-01` etc.) since `cafefcb`, which is expected — `cafefcb` is a fixed checkpoint SHA, not a moving target. No drift, no regression.
  - **Prettier tie-breaker (third independent run)**: `npx prettier --check "app/(public)/_components/vendor-url.ts"` in the main repo (not an isolated worktree) → `"All matched files use Prettier code style!"` — **passes**. Installed version this run: `npx prettier --version` → `3.8.5` — notably a *third* distinct version observation across the three checks in this dispute (Team-1's original: `3.8.5`; re-entered Review-A: `3.9.1`; this run: `3.8.5`), yet the result is unanimous PASS across all three. This weakens rather than strengthens the version-drift hypothesis recorded above — the formatting holds across multiple prettier point-releases, so it isn't fragile to the exact resolved patch version. (Did not run `prettier --write` against the tracked file — the harness correctly declined that as an unauthorized destructive action against committed source; `--check` alone is sufficient and non-destructive for this verification.)
  - **Version-independent cross-check**: manual byte count of the single-line union form (`export type VendorSubpage = "about" | "products" | "projects" | "industries" | "contact" | "resources";`) → 103 characters, confirmed via `wc -c`, matching the re-entered Review-A's independent count. This is over the pinned `printWidth: 100` regardless of which prettier binary is asked, so the 6-line wrap is mandatory output, not a stylistic choice — a fourth independent method converging on the same conclusion.
  - **Spot-checks** (not a full re-run of the first Review-B's empirical suite, per this re-check's scope): `npx eslint` on `vendor-url.ts` plus three other touched files (`vendors/[slug]/page.tsx`, `vendor-microsite-footer.tsx`, `vendor-microsite-navigation.tsx`) → exit 0, clean. `npx tsc --noEmit` → no errors reported against `vendor-url.ts` or the vendor-microsite files. Both match the commit message's "tsc/eslint/prettier green" claim.
  - **Conclusion**: three independent reviewers (Team-1's own investigation, the re-entered Review-A, and this re-check Review-B), across four total prettier invocations and three different observed prettier versions, unanimously confirm the committed file conforms to this repo's formatting rules. The original Review-B MINOR does not hold — it was an isolated-worktree environment artifact, not a defect in the committed code. No new findings surfaced. BLOCKER=0 · MAJOR=0 · MINOR=0 on both lanes, same checkpoint SHA (`cafefcb`).
  - **Verdict: PASS.** Per Amendment v1.3, A:PASS ∧ B:PASS (B/M/M=0) on the same checkpoint SHA is itself the approval signal — no further owner turn required for this clean pass. RV-0128 review cycle is closed; FE-PUB-10 is ready for Dev-team milestone-close commit (`milestone(FE-PUB-10): close — RV-0128 A:PASS B:PASS`) per §13's Dev-team self-close provision.

### RV-0134 · BX-04 · Buyer sidebar Information Architecture (canonical, owner-directed) · Team-2
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Lane G (shared-shell type/component extension + 6 new buyer routes — architecture-adjacent: extends the cross-workspace `NavItem`/`Sidebar`/`MobileNav`, though additively). Owner directive, verbatim scope: "treat the sidebar as the canonical Buyer Information Architecture… build the complete sidebar exactly as designed… missing pages should be scaffolded, not omitted… do not invent business logic or fake data… rename Archived RFQs to Closed RFQs."
- **Reuse audit first** (owner: "check if possible — all items should be reusable"), against the frozen `page_inventory.md` + the real route tree: 8 of the 24 sidebar leaves are direct reuse of already-built, already-approved pages (Dashboard, My RFQs, Vendor Directory, Notifications — `/notifications` existed but was never nav-mounted, Board standing agenda #8 — Team/Organization/Profile/Settings); 2 reuse `/rfqs` via a query-param filter (`Draft Requests` → `?state=draft`, a REAL frozen Doc-4M RFQ state); `Archived RFQs` renamed **`Closed RFQs`** per the owner's decision 4, since no single frozen state named "archived" exists (closest honest grouping is `closed_won ∪ closed_lost ∪ expired ∪ cancelled`, not a single state to filter on presentation-only today — the label change is applied, the underlying filter wiring is deferred with everything else GI-02). 4 already-shipped, already-approved pages the mockup didn't name — **Approvals** (P-BUY-12), **Engagements** (P-BUY-19), **Documents** (P-DOC-01), **Vendor CRM** (P-BUY-26/27) — are folded into the nearest matching group rather than dropped from the nav (removing a live milestone's only entry point would be a silent regression, not a redesign; not authorized by the owner's decision). The remaining 8 leaves (Received Quotes, Compare Quotes, Active Orders, Order History, Saved Vendors, Specification Library, Messages, Reports & Analytics) have zero backing contract/page anywhere in the frozen corpus — per decision 5/6, these are **scaffolded, not omitted**.
- **Shared shell extension** (`app/(app)/_components/shell/`): `types.ts` — `NavItem.children?: NavItem[]`, additive/optional, same pattern as BX-03's `search` field; a set `children` renders the item as a non-interactive group header (icon + label, its own `href` unused/never an `<a>`) with an indented child list, mirroring the mockup's "RFQs / My RFQs / Draft Requests / Closed RFQs" tree — a workspace that never sets it (vendor/admin/account) renders exactly as before. `sidebar.tsx` + `mobile-nav.tsx` both refactored into `NavLink`/`NavGroup` sub-components implementing this (desktop + mobile drawer both updated, kept behaviorally identical for flat sections). `icons.ts` — 3 new keys (`notifications`→Bell, `messages`→MessageSquare, `reports`→BarChart3), additive.
- **Buyer nav model rewrite** (`(buyer)/_components/buyer-nav-model.ts`): full re-group Dashboard / Procurement (RFQs·Quotations·Purchase Orders groups + Documents) / Marketplace (Vendor Directory·Saved Vendors·Specification Library·Vendor CRM) / Communication (Messages·Notifications) / Analytics (Reports & Analytics) / Organization (Team·Organization) / Account (Profile·Settings).
- **6 new scaffold routes**, each a `page.tsx` (Server Component, no hooks/fetch) composing ONE new shared buyer-scoped `ImplementationPendingView` (`(buyer)/_components/implementation-pending-view.tsx` — Breadcrumbs + PageHeader + kit `EmptyState`, no new kit primitive) — `quotations` (Received Quotes) · `quotations/compare` (Compare Quotes) · `purchase-orders` (Active Orders / Order History, via `?status=` — copy only, no data) · `saved-vendors` · `spec-library` · `messages` · `reports`. Each page's own header comment states exactly which frozen read is missing (per owner decision 2: "do not invent business logic or fake data" — none of the 6 render a filter bar/action bar, since there is no real contract-backed filter/action to offer yet; a disabled placeholder toolbar was judged a bigger fabrication risk [GI-12] than omitting it, page-level judgment call, flagged here for the record).
- **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit` project-wide clean; `eslint .` project-wide clean; `prettier --check` clean (one pre-existing formatting drift in the edited `sidebar.tsx`, `prettier --write`'d before commit — no other files touched). Live-rendered on a fresh `next dev`: all 22 nav-linked routes 200 (incl. the two `?state=` RFQ filters and both `?status=` PO views); grep-confirmed all 24 sidebar labels present exactly once each on `/dashboard`, zero occurrences of "Archived" anywhere. Regression: `/workspace` (vendor) and `/admin` both still 200, vendor nav grep-confirmed to show none of the new buyer-only labels (nav model isolation intact). Mobile drawer (390px, Playwright interaction — opened the real `Sheet`, read its rendered text): full nested tree renders identically to the desktop sidebar (Procurement/Marketplace/Communication/Analytics/Organization/Account groups, all children indented under their parent). Axe: 0 violations desktop across `/dashboard`, `/quotations`, `/saved-vendors`, `/purchase-orders`; 1 mobile-only violation, confirmed the same pre-existing shell `quick-create` `button-name` defect already tracked at RV-0129/RV-0133/Board standing agenda #11 — not introduced here.

### RV-0135 · BX-05 · Accordion sidebar + shell-persistence bug fix (P-BUY-01 nav) · Team-2
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Lane G (shared-shell behavior change + 4 new buyer-mounted composition pages + 1 relocated shared page). Owner bug report, verbatim: "sidebar should be collapsible; one open, other close" + "BUG FIX — Preserve Dashboard Shell — clicking Messages, Notifications, Reports & Analytics, Team, Organization, Profile, and Settings navigates outside the dashboard shell," with acceptance criteria (no shell leave, sidebar/topbar never remount, URL stays under the buyer surface, active-nav highlighting works).
- **Root-cause verified empirically before fixing anything** (a DOM probe attached to the sidebar's own node, then real Playwright clicks through every named nav item — not an assumption): of the 7 items named in the bug report, only **5 actually remount** — `/notifications`, `/account/members` (Team), `/account/organization`, `/account/profile`, `/account/settings` each sit OUTSIDE the `(buyer)` route group with their OWN `layout.tsx` mounting a DIFFERENT `ShellViewModel` (generic `ACCOUNT_NAV`, different identity/breadcrumb) — a real Next.js layout-tree remount. **Messages and Reports & Analytics do NOT remount** — both already live inside `(buyer)/`, correctly built at BX-04; included in the bug report in error, verified and reported back rather than "fixed" a second time.
- **Rejected the literal proposed remedy** (move every buyer route under a `/dashboard/*` URL prefix inheriting a literal `app/dashboard/layout.tsx`): no such file exists in this codebase (the real mechanism is the `(buyer)` route GROUP, which is intentionally invisible in the URL — the idiomatic Next.js way to share a layout without adding a path segment); renaming would touch ~25 already-shipped, already-approved `P-BUY-*` routes and every internal link/breadcrumb across them, for zero benefit beyond what a narrower fix already achieves. Used the SAME proven fix this exact codebase already applied to the identical problem on the Vendor track (`FE-VEN-10/11/12`, Board-ruled Option B, composition-not-fork): new buyer-mounted pages compose the EXISTING, UNMODIFIED Account view components inside the persistent Buyer shell, rather than linking out to `/account/*`.
- **Fix — 5 remounting items**:
  - `(buyer)/team/page.tsx` composes `MembersView` (P-ACC-06) — unmodified, zero props.
  - `(buyer)/organization/page.tsx` composes `OrganizationProfile` (P-ACC-04) — unmodified; `OrganizationLifecycle` not composed (not in the requested sidebar, not fabricated).
  - `(buyer)/profile/page.tsx` composes `UserProfileForm` (P-ACC-02) — unmodified.
  - `(buyer)/settings/page.tsx` composes `SecuritySettings` (P-ACC-03) + `NotificationPreferences` (P-ACC-15) via a new buyer-scoped `BuyerWorkspaceTabs` (2 tabs — NOT 3 like the vendor's, since the buyer sidebar already has a separate "Profile" nav item, so bundling Profile here too would duplicate it). `BuyerWorkspaceTabs` duplicates the vendor track's `_components/vendor/shared/workspace-tabs.tsx` at the same narrow scope rather than importing it — Review-A convention across this whole program is zero `_components/vendor/*` import under `(buyer)/`.
  - `/notifications` (P-SH-02, a shared shell page) was **relocated bodily** into `(buyer)/notifications/` at the SAME URL (route groups don't affect the path — no link anywhere needed to change) rather than composed a second time: its own `layout.tsx` header comment already flagged the shell placement as unresolved ("not settled in the corpus... flagged for Team-4"), and a repo-wide grep found ZERO non-buyer references to `/notifications` — buyer was its only real consumer, so this resolves the open question in the direction the evidence already pointed. The old top-level `app/(app)/notifications/` (page + layout + seed) is deleted, not left dangling. `(buyer)/layout.tsx` now feeds the SAME seed into `ShellViewModel.notifications`/`unreadCount` so the topbar bell dropdown stays consistent with the full page, exactly as before the move.
  - The original `/account/members|organization|profile|settings` routes are UNTOUCHED — Account stays the canonical surface for anyone landing there directly (e.g. via a cross-workspace link); these are additional, not replacement, entry points.
- **Fix — accordion sidebar**: shared shell `Sidebar`/`MobileNav` both refactored — a group header (e.g. "RFQs") is now a `<button aria-expanded>` with a chevron, not inert `<div>` text; single `openGroup: string | null` state per component instance implements "one open, other close" (clicking a different group's header closes whichever was open; clicking the same header again closes it). Navigating into a group's child page auto-opens that group on mount/route-change (`findActiveGroupLabel`, re-derived via `useEffect` on `[nav, pathname, search]`).
- **Real bug caught and fixed during verification, not shipped**: the pre-existing `isActive(pathname, href)` compared ONLY `usePathname()` (which never includes the query string) against `href` — so every query-param filter child (`Draft Requests` → `/rfqs?state=draft`, `Closed RFQs`, `Active Orders`, `Order History`) silently never matched, meaning neither the "active" highlight NOR the accordion auto-open would ever fire for those four links. Caught by an end-to-end Playwright check (not just a visual glance) BEFORE this was reported as done. Fixed by adding `useSearchParams()` and an exact-path+exact-query comparison for query-bearing hrefs (falling back to the original prefix-match behavior for query-less hrefs, so `/rfqs/123`-style nested detail routes still correctly activate a parent `/rfqs`-style link). Re-verified live: `/purchase-orders?status=active` → "Purchase Orders" group auto-opens, "Active Orders" shows `aria-current="page"`; `/rfqs?state=draft` → "RFQs" group opens, "Draft Requests" active; bare `/rfqs` → "My RFQs" active, not "Draft Requests".
- **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit` project-wide clean; `eslint .` project-wide clean; all 15 touched/new routes live 200 (`/messages` `/reports` `/notifications` `/team` `/organization` `/profile` `/settings` + the 4 new/existing query-param variants + the untouched `/account/*` originals, confirmed still 200 standalone). **Remount probe re-run with the actual sidebar links** (DOM attribute survival test, not a visual check): all 7 originally-reported items now `survived=true`. Accordion Playwright-verified: opening RFQs → `["RFQs"]`; opening Quotations → `["Quotations"]` (RFQs auto-closed); clicking Quotations again → `[]` (closed). Mobile drawer (390px) re-verified with the same accordion behavior, byte-consistent with desktop. Axe: 0 violations on `/dashboard`, `/rfqs?state=draft`, `/team`, `/organization`, `/profile`, `/notifications`; **1 pre-existing `color-contrast` violation on `/settings`**, traced into the reused `SecuritySettings` component's "deactivate account" copy — independently reproduced on the ORIGINAL, completely untouched `/account/security` page, confirming it is NOT introduced by this composition (same disclosure class as the tracked `quick-create` a11y bug — real, pre-existing, out of Team-2's ownership of that shared Account component, not fixed unilaterally). Regression: `/workspace` (vendor) and `/admin` axe-clean, 0 violations, confirming the shared shell changes (accordion, `isActive` fix) don't affect vendor/admin nav (neither defines any `children` group, so `NavGroup`/accordion code paths never execute for them).
- Governance: no coined RFQ/PO state (accordion + active-state fixes are pure presentation-logic corrections, no new field); Inv#11 preserved (Vendor CRM untouched, no status leak); composition-not-fork honored throughout (every reused Account component rendered unmodified, zero props changed); no frozen-kit primitive duplicated (`BuyerWorkspaceTabs` wraps the same kit `Tabs` the vendor's `WorkspaceTabs` already wraps, at buyer's own narrow scope, per the established zero-cross-import convention); shared shell extension (`useSearchParams`, accordion state) additive/behavioral-fix only, no type/contract change beyond BX-04's already-reviewed `children` field.
- Disposition: dev-team self-close (Team-2) — no BLOCKER/MAJOR/MINOR found; the one real defect this pass surfaced (`isActive` ignoring query strings) was caught and fixed BEFORE being reported as complete, not left for a reviewer to find.
- Board: not required (Amendment v1.3 §13 — clean verification, no BLOCKER/MAJOR/MINOR/REGRESSION/Flag-and-Halt; owner-directed bug-fix scope, not a self-initiated architecture change). Result: ✅ **Closed** — BX-05, all 7 originally-reported navigation items now confirmed to stay inside the persistent Buyer shell; accordion sidebar live on desktop + mobile.

### RV-0136 · BX-06 · Dashboard font-size/spacing/card-style pass (P-BUY-01) · Team-2
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Lane L (typography/spacing-only presentation delta on `KpiStatCard` + the dashboard `WelcomeBand`, no new page, no contract/data surface touched). Owner request: "check the folder `buyer-dashboard-layout` for the dashboard? if possible, make our dashboard like this in color, font size, style."
- **Source investigated**: `buyer-dashboard-layout/` is a standalone v0-generated design-reference project (own `package.json`/registry, not installed in this workspace), staged for commit separately from this work. Its own `registry/common/globals.css` is explicitly self-disclosed as **"external evaluation source only — does NOT resolve DEF-03 for the repo"** and uses an Indigo-primary palette (`--primary: #4f46e5`) predating this repo's owner-directed 2026-06-30 Navy-dominant brand migration (memory: "purple footprint cut ~80%").
- **Color decision escalated to the owner** (a real, consequential re-skin call, not a mechanical tweak) rather than silently reverting a ratified, WCAG-tested brand decision or silently ignoring the "color" part of the request: owner chose **keep Navy, match everything else** — adopt the reference's font sizes/spacing/card layout, render through the existing Navy-dominant token system, stay visually consistent with every other already-shipped page.
- **Style changes applied** (`(buyer)/_components/kpi-stat-card.tsx`, `(buyer)/dashboard/dashboard-view.tsx`, both already buyer-scoped Tier-2 compositions — no shared-kit file touched): KPI value text `text-2xl`→`text-3xl` + `tabular-nums`; icon badge `size-8`→`size-9`, icon glyph `size-4`→`size-5`; card padding `p-4`→`p-5`; label text `text-xs`→`text-sm`; `WelcomeBand` greeting `text-lg`→`text-xl tracking-tight`; KPI grid `grid-cols-2 xl:grid-cols-4` → mobile-first `grid-cols-1 sm:grid-cols-2 xl:grid-cols-4`. Existing `TONE_ICON_BOX` (Navy/info/success/warning) left untouched — no color-token change anywhere.
- **Real regression caught and fixed during verification, not shipped**: the bigger `text-3xl` value broke the "Spend" KPI card — a long `BDT 18,450,000.00` currency string overflowed its CSS Grid cell (Grid items default to `min-width: auto`, i.e. their content's intrinsic width, so a long unbroken value doesn't shrink to the track) and visually spilled past the card's right edge. Caught via an actual full-page screenshot comparison, not just a code read. Fixed with `min-w-0` on the `Card` wrapper + `break-words leading-tight` on the value container, so long values now wrap onto a second line inside their own card instead of overflowing. Re-screenshotted to confirm: desktop, mobile (390px), and the OTHER `KpiStatCard` consumer (`quotation-detail-view.tsx`'s "Quoted amount"/"Received" cards, FE-BUY-04) all render correctly with the fix — the second consumer wasn't passed `icon`/`tone` before and still isn't, purely backward-compatible.
- **Hygiene fix (adjacent, disclosed)**: the newly-staged `buyer-dashboard-layout/` folder (its own uninstalled deps) was being picked up by the root `tsc --noEmit` (497 errors) and `eslint .` (5 errors/14 warnings) glob, none of it this repo's own code. Added it to `tsconfig.json`'s `exclude` and `eslint.config.mjs`'s `ignores` — a one-line hygiene fix so project-wide gates report only this repo's own conformance again; did not touch anything inside the reference folder itself.
- **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit` clean (0 errors, down from 497 pollution-errors); `eslint .` clean (0, down from 5 errors/14 warnings); `prettier --check` clean. Full-page Playwright screenshots at 1440×900 and 390×844 confirm the KPI band, welcome band, and sidebar all render as intended, no clipping/overflow anywhere on the page. Axe: 0 violations on `/dashboard` desktop and the quotation-detail page; 1 pre-existing mobile `button-name` violation (the already-tracked shell `quick-create` bug, Board agenda #11) — unrelated, not introduced.
- Governance: no color-token change (Navy-dominant system untouched, owner-confirmed); no coined field/figure (pure typography/spacing); composition-not-fork preserved (`KpiStatCard` remains the same buyer-scoped Tier-2 composition, not a new kit primitive); `buyer-dashboard-layout/` itself was NOT modified, only excluded from tooling glob.
- Disposition: dev-team self-close (Team-2) — no BLOCKER/MAJOR/MINOR found; the one real regression this pass surfaced (KPI value overflow) was caught and fixed before being reported as complete.
- Board: not required for the style delta (Amendment v1.3 §13 — clean verification, no BLOCKER/MAJOR/MINOR/REGRESSION/Flag-and-Halt); the one real product decision embedded in this request (color) WAS escalated live to the owner rather than decided unilaterally. Result: ✅ **Closed** — BX-06, dashboard KPI/welcome-band typography and spacing now match the reference's density/weight while staying on the ratified Navy palette.

### RV-0136 addendum · BX-06 round 2 · Structural layout correction · Team-2
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Owner feedback on the first pass: **"but the layout is unchanged."** Diagnosed honestly rather than assumed: first suspected/blamed a corrupted dev-server build cache (several of this session's own test `next dev` instances on other ports had, in fact, been left running and sharing the same `.next` cache — a real, separate problem, cleaned up: killed the orphaned processes, cleared `.next`, restarted the owner's port-3000 server on request) — but a direct check of the RENDERED HTML (not a naive grep, which was double-counting matches inside the React Server Component hydration payload) proved the round-1 typography changes were live and correct the whole time. The actual feedback was accurate on its own terms: round 1 only resized existing elements and never changed the page's STRUCTURE, which is why it still read as "the same dashboard."
- **Escalated the two structural gaps explicitly** (both are real product decisions, not mechanical tweaks) rather than guessing: **(1)** KPI trend badges — the reference's deltas ("+3 this week") are its OWN illustrative-only placeholders (its `page.tsx`: *"Values/trends are illustrative only"*), and no frozen trend/delta read exists anywhere in the corpus (`view-models.ts`'s own header: *"every field traces to a frozen contract field... no state is invented"*); **(2)** a bundled utility header card (org switcher + search + notifications + messages + profile) duplicates controls the shell topbar already renders live on every page. Owner chose **both**, informed of the duplication trade-off on (2).
- **KPI trend badges**: new `KpiTrend` capability on `KpiStatCard` (`trend?: {label, direction}`) — a `Badge` + `TrendingUp`/`TrendingDown` icon + sr-only "Increase of/Decrease of " text (direction never color-only, GI-06). Kept OUT of the contract-traced `BuyerDashboardKpis` interface (would have violated that file's own "coins no contract" framing) — wired instead as a UI-layer decoration directly in `dashboard-view.tsx`, the same precedent already used for the "Awaiting my approval" card's hardcoded "Review queue" caption link. Gated on the real KPI value being present — never rendered next to a "—" placeholder. Explicitly disclosed in code comments as illustrative presentation-fixture content standing in for a future wired comparison read, the same disclosure posture the rest of this page's SEED already carries (not a new governance exception).
- **Bundled utility header**: `WelcomeBand` renamed/expanded to `DashboardHeaderCard` — one bordered `Card` containing an org-context chip, a `/discover` search link, and `Bell`/`MessageSquare`/profile icon links (all real routes: `/notifications`, `/messages`, `/profile`), followed by the existing "Welcome back" greeting. Deliberately built as PLAIN NAVIGATION LINKS, not a second live `DropdownMenu` instance — avoids stacking two independent interactive/focus-trap widgets (org-switcher, notification dropdown, profile menu) on one page, while still visually matching the reference's utility-row-plus-greeting structure. Disclosed inline as a deliberate, owner-confirmed duplication of topbar functionality.
- **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit` clean; `eslint .` clean; `prettier --check` clean. Fresh Playwright screenshots (1440×950, 390×844) against a clean dev server confirm: 3 of 4 KPI cards now show a trend badge (the 4th, "Awaiting my approval", keeps its existing "Review queue" caption instead — no double-decoration); the header card renders the full utility row + greeting on desktop and wraps cleanly to two rows on mobile; sidebar/topbar unaffected. Axe: 0 violations desktop; 1 pre-existing mobile `button-name` violation (the same tracked shell `quick-create` bug, Board agenda #11) — the 3 new icon links (`Notifications`/`Messages`/`Profile`) all carry explicit `aria-label`s and introduce no new violations.
- Governance: `trend` kept out of the typed contract interface (UI-decoration only, explicitly disclosed as illustrative, gated on real-value presence, never shown as authoritative); non-disclosure/R6/R7 otherwise unaffected (no new counts, no ranking, no excluded-vendor signal); composition-not-fork preserved (icon links point at real existing routes, no new page).
- Disposition: dev-team self-close (Team-2). Both structural gaps the owner named are now genuinely addressed, not just resized text.
- Board: not required (Amendment v1.3 §13); both real product-decision points (trend fabrication risk, topbar duplication) were escalated live to the owner before building, per the same discipline as the original color escalation. Result: ✅ **Closed** — the dashboard's structural layout, not just its typography, now matches the reference's density and composition.

### RV-0137 · VX-01 · Vendor Dashboard + sidebar nav redesign (P-VND-01/all) · Team-3
- Date: 2026-07-03 · Lane G (new sidebar taxonomy + a full dashboard-page content rebuild; owner-directed, delivered as a verbatim mockup screenshot, verified by Team-3 in lieu of the normal Dev→A→B pipeline — same posture as Team-2's BX-04..06). Owner request: "this should be our vendor dashboard, replace the existing vendor dashboard with these."
- **Three governance conflicts flagged before building, adjudicated by the owner:** (1) a "Mushok Challan" nav item reintroduces the still-open `ESC-OPS-DOC-MUSHOK` gap (unmodeled Bangladesh VAT documents); (2) an "Increase Score" button + "+25 points" mechanic on a Trust Score card directly conflicts with the already-verified R5 no-mutation invariant ("no Edit Trust Score can ever exist... no action anywhere", confirmed at FE-VEN-09's close) and the Board's own "never show formula" rule; (3) "Gold/Platinum" tier badges don't map to any real corpus concept (Financial Tier is A–E; Trust Center bands are Unverified/Building trust/Trusted/Highly trusted/Elite). Presented via `AskUserQuestion` (style-only vs. literal vs. per-item clarification) — **owner chose "build it literally as shown."**
- **Resolution applied per conflict** (built literally per the ruling, without violating the underlying invariants): (1) "Mushok Challan" nav entry exists as directed, scaffolded via a new vendor-local `ImplementationPendingView` (mirrors the buyer BX-04 component — not cross-imported, workspace-boundary discipline) that discloses the `ESC-OPS-DOC-MUSHOK` gap plainly; no VAT document kind, format, or coined slug fabricated anywhere. (2) "Increase Score" is a plain navigation `Link` to the real Company Profile page — it does not submit/edit/mutate the trust score itself (the score stays System-computed only); the "+25 points" formula-exposure was softened to a non-numeric nudge ("may improve your score") since the Board's ruling explicitly forbids showing "formula". (3) Gold/Platinum built as a NEW, dashboard-only presentation concept, explicitly commented as distinct from (and never cross-mutating) `FinancialTier`/the Trust Center's band vocabulary — reuses the real `TrustScoreRing` for the underlying 0–100 number (permitted per the Board's 2026-07-03 Trust Score display ruling), never fabricates a second score.

- **KPI stat tiles** (Total RFQs/Active Quotes/New POs/Messages): built as a disclosed presentation-fixture SEED, mirroring the buyer track's own `KpiStatCard` governance posture exactly (`(buyer)/_components/kpi-stat-card.tsx` — "every figure is a WIRED READ... never client-computed") — a new vendor-scoped `VendorKpiStatCard`, not a cross-workspace import. New icon keys added to the shared registry: `showcase`, `inquiries`, `award` (Trophy) — additive, no existing key repurposed.
- **Real shared-shell bug caught and fixed during verification, not shipped**: both `Sidebar` and `MobileNav` set `aria-controls={panelId}` on a nav-group toggle unconditionally, but the referenced `<ul id={panelId}>` only renders when that specific group is open — since only one group can be open at a time (single `openGroup` state), a CLOSED sibling group's button pointed `aria-controls` at a non-existent id (`aria-valid-attr-value`, axe-critical). Latent since BX-04 introduced `NavItem.children`, but never triggered until VX-01 put two sibling single-item groups (Digital Showcase, Business Docs) on the same page. Fixed in both files: `aria-controls` now only set when the panel will actually render. Live-reverified in an isolated worktree — violation gone.
- **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit`/`eslint`/`prettier --check` all clean across every new/changed file. Live-rendered in an isolated `git worktree` (real `npm install`, own dev server): all 20 nav destinations return 200 (including the 4 new scaffolded pages and the 2 real `?stage=` filtered links into the FE-DOC-02 hub); rendered dashboard HTML confirms all 4 KPI numbers, the Gold/Platinum tier labels, and every new nav label render correctly; grep confirms zero "+25"/point-delta text leaked anywhere. - **Builder judgment calls (a)–(e) — Team-4 adjudication (disposition proposals; Board rules):**
  - **(a) No per-row `inngest.send`; delivery = the status transition; Inngest = pump with distinct dispatch/archive steps → ACCEPT (faithful §B6 reading).** §B6 nowhere mandates a broker handoff: the worker "IS the delivery mechanism" (Trigger, line 409), its effect is captured under Mutation-Scope `pending → dispatched`, and the Response Contract observes outcome via "consumer effects and ops telemetry" (line 417). With zero consumers in existence (per-event integration contracts are producing-module-authored per §4.4 — none exist; M0/M1 emit zero §8 events, `[DC-1]`), the transition is the complete delivery today. The distinct-durable-steps shape realizes both scheduled triggers (dispatch poll + retention sweep) distinctly per Doc-8B §7.2. Rider recorded as OBS-4 below.
  - **(b) DLQ alerting = returned counters, no console/external sink → ACCEPT (faithful).** §B6 line 446: "park the row (retain in `pending` with attempts at max) and raise an ops alert per core.outbox_dlq_policy … Never silently drop"; §17.1 classes this as operational telemetry. Parking verified (rows retained `pending` at ceiling, excluded from advancement, delete-blocked by trigger); the counters + governing `dlqPolicy` value surfaced on the durable step output are not silent; no ops-alert-sink contract exists anywhere in the corpus to bind to (`src/shared/telemetry` checked — placeholder). Wiring a real sink is future work under whatever authority defines one.
  - **(c) `*_dedup_window` POLICY keys not read → ACCEPT (faithful).** §B6 line 438 states verbatim that the status transition is the dedup guard; a permanent transition is strictly stronger than any time window, so the Window declarations (`core.outbox_dispatch_dedup_window` line 436 / `core.outbox_archive_dedup_window` line 519) leave the worker no windowed mechanic to execute — both keys remain seeded (migration lines 266/269) and declaratively bound. Caveat: the builder's gloss calling them "consumer-idempotency windows" is imprecise (the Window field sits on the workers' OWN Idempotency blocks); if a windowed mechanic is ever wanted, it needs an authority definition first — never a local widening.
  - **(d) Reconciliation folded into the dispatch worker, not a third contract-ID → ACCEPT (verbatim-correct).** §B6 defines exactly two workers (line 381: "a dispatcher worker and an archival worker") and places Reconciliation as a bullet of the dispatch contract's "Delivery, Retry & Reconciliation (operational — §15.6, §16.2, §16.8)" section (line 447). A third contract-ID would have been the invention.
  - **(e) WP-1.8 archival test UPDATED → ACCEPT (conformant hardening, not a masked regression).** The old expectation (unconditional archival of a just-dispatched row) contradicted §B6's Archive Request Contract (only rows with `dispatched_at` older than `core.outbox_archive_retention`, line 498). The new test asserts strictly more: fresh-dispatched NOT archived + backdated row archived + the ORIGINAL terminal-idempotency assertion retained (current file lines 163–165). The prior green pinned pre-hardening behavior, now corrected to the frozen spec.
- **Findings:**
  1. **[NIT] `src/modules/core/infrastructure/events/outbox-policy.ts:122`** — `dlqPolicyParks()` is exported but never called anywhere in the repo (dead export). Either consume it (e.g. assert the park posture when counting `deadLettered`) or drop it at a future M0 checkpoint. Non-gating.
  2. **[OBS]** Reconciliation counts `attempts ∈ [1, max)` where §B6 line 447 says "attempts < max": an `attempts = 0` row can never be observed stuck by a running worker (always immediately dispatch-eligible in the same pass), so the narrowing is sound. Noted alongside: a backoff-saturated batch (`take: batchSize` consumed by ineligible rows) can defer a fresh row one tick — bounded by the POLICY backoff cap, self-healing, no conformance issue.
  3. **[OBS]** `deadLettered` / `reconciledStuck` are standing gauges (a parked row is re-counted every pass until operationally resolved) — a reasonable never-silent posture for a parked backlog; when a real ops sink is wired it should alert on depth, not novelty.
  4. **[OBS]** (rider to (a)) transition-as-delivery is complete ONLY while zero consumers exist; the first real consumer contract requires a transport-leg WP under its own authority — never a silent widening of these workers.

  - **Test discrimination (adversarial replay, analytic — the W2-CORE-1 B-1 standard, no sabotage committed):** every 8B assertion is row-scoped to a fresh UUIDv7 fixture (cannot pass vacuously off other rows; run counters asserted `>= 1` only, per the append-only table). The backoff case kills both the "ignores backoff" mutant (first phase would observe `dispatched`) and the "never elapses" mutant (second phase would stay `pending`, attempts pinned exactly). The dead-letter case deliberately ELAPSES backoff (updatedAgo 10m) so an `lte`-ceiling off-by-one would dispatch the row and fail the row-level pins — park is asserted at row level (retained `pending`, attempts = the live seeded POLICY max, row not null ⇒ never dropped), not counter-only, and `dlqPolicy` is equality-checked against the seeded row (no restated value). The retention case kills the unconditional-archival AND no-archival mutants (fresh `dispatched` untouched + 400-day-backdated row archived). Time is manipulated via stored timestamps (staff-context raw `updated_at`/`dispatched_at` backdates) — zero sleeps, no seeded clock needed. 8F: the rollback case aborts via a typed sentinel and asserts BOTH rows absent (no phantom emit); the commit case proves the emitted row enters the real dispatch lifecycle. The pre-existing WP-1.8 idempotency pins retain real power (attempts stays 1 + `dispatchedAt` unchanged on re-run). Weak spot (non-gating): the archival-idempotency case (`outbox-dispatch-hardening.test.ts:200–206`) has low mutant-killing power — `archived` is terminal and DB-trigger-enforced regardless of worker behavior.
  - **Implementation quality:** `drain-outbox.service.ts` EXTENDED, not forked — legacy `drainOutbox` now composes the two §B6 workers (single implementation, stable compat shape). The WP-1.8 literal fallback `DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 1` was REMOVED in favor of fail-loud POLICY reads — a quality gain: a POLICY-read failure aborts the whole single-transaction pass → Inngest step failure → clean retry; no partial advancement is possible. Counters are truthful single-threaded (`dispatched`/`archived` count actual row updates; `deadLettered`/`reconciledStuck` are pre-pass gauges per OBS-3). The Inngest function realizes two DISTINCT durable steps as claimed; step retries re-run a fully-transactional idempotent pass, and the per-row POLICY backoff keys off `updated_at` — independent of Inngest's retry cadence, no harmful doubling.
  - **B-1 [MINOR]** `src/modules/core/infrastructure/events/drain-outbox.service.ts:130–133` (dispatch) · `:168–171` (archive) — the advance writes use `update({ where: { id } })` with NO source-status recheck: the §B6 dedup guard is enforced at SELECT time only, not WRITE time. Under concurrent invocation (the Inngest function has cron + `core/outbox.drain.requested` triggers and no `concurrency` limit; Prisma interactive tx = READ COMMITTED, and EvalPlanQual re-checks only `id = X`), two overlapping passes can both process the same `pending` row: the loser's write lands as a same-state `dispatched → dispatched` update — expressly ADMITTED by the forward-only trigger ("same-state idempotent", `core_init` migration line 47) and untouched by the payload-immutability trigger (TG_ARGV excludes status/attempts/dispatched_at) — double-incrementing `attempts`, overwriting `dispatched_at` (the archival-retention anchor), and double-counting `dispatched` across the two results. This falsifies the in-diff claim (`inngest/functions/dispatch-outbox.ts:15–16`: "overlapping ticks and step retries advance nothing twice") — the WP-1.8-proven idempotency pins (attempts stay 1, `dispatchedAt` unchanged) hold single-threaded only; the race is never exercised. Containment (why MINOR, not MAJOR): the transition itself still occurs exactly once (no double delivery — delivery IS the transition, zero consumers exist); no row lost, no illegal transition, no payload mutation; the write pattern is inherited verbatim from WP-1.8 and no nudge sender exists yet, so the overlap is practically unreachable TODAY — but this is the hardening WP and it re-asserts the safety claim in new text. Fix (compare-and-set): `updateMany({ where: { id: row.id, status: "pending" }, data: … })` and count `.count` (archive leg symmetric with `status: "dispatched"`), making counters truthful and the claim real; optionally `concurrency: { limit: 1 }` on the Inngest function. Foldable into the next M0 checkpoint alongside NIT-1.
  - **B-2 [NIT]** `tests/integration/outbox-dispatch-hardening.test.ts:125–133` — the backoff "not yet elapsed" phase rests on an implicit ~2s real-clock margin (the seeded base backoff) between seeding and the first pass; a cold-engine/slow-CI stall beyond the base delay fails it spuriously (flake-to-FAIL only — it can never vacuously pass). Widen: seed `attempts` near the POLICY ceiling so the governing delay is the backoff CAP (minutes), staying value-agnostic.
  - **B-3 [NIT]** 8B edge gaps: (i) the last-permitted-attempt boundary `attempts = max − 1` (backoff elapsed) is never pinned as still-eligible — a premature-park off-by-one (`lt: maxAttempts − 1`) would pass every current test (the at-ceiling side IS pinned by the dead-letter case); (ii) the contract input `batchSize` is unexercised on both workers (the OBS-2 batch-saturation semantics are entirely untested). One `attempts = max − 1` case + one `batchSize: 1` case closes both.
  - Governance/security sweep (route-to-A duty): nothing new — no payload read/log, boundaries clean, no coined key/event/status value; Team-6 N/A independently re-confirmed on this pass.
  - **Disposition proposal (Raise ≠ Accept — author/Board rule):** B-1 → Agent M0 compare-and-set patch at a follow-up checkpoint (fold in NIT-1 dead export), delta-only re-verify; B-2/B-3 deferrable into the same patch. Gate B/M/M = 0 NOT met at this SHA — no clean-gate close until B-1 is adjudicated (and, if accepted, patched + re-verified). 0 false positives claimed: the race admission path was verified against the trigger DDL, the Prisma where-clause, and the isolation level — not assumed.

Write-site sweep of the full service confirms the builder's claim: dead-letter (`:96–98`) and reconciliation (`:103–109`) are `count()` gauges ONLY — the two CAS `updateMany` calls are the sole writes in either worker.

Discriminating: under READ COMMITTED, the blocked CAS write's EvalPlanQual re-check re-evaluates `status = 'pending'` against the racer-committed row version → matches ZERO rows (no-op); the OLD `update({ where: { id } })` re-checks `id` only → the same-state `dispatched → dispatched` write LANDS (admitted-as-idempotent by the forward-only trigger per the B-1 analysis) → `attempts` → 2 and `dispatched_at` → the worker's later `now`, failing BOTH pins (`attempts` === 1 · `dispatchedAt` === the racer's earlier timestamp). Every possible misordering is loud (poll throws, or the attempts pin fails — no path lets the old form pass), confirming the builder's revert-fail/restore-pass claim analytically. Attempts-0 seeding is immediately backoff-eligible (RV-0144 OBS-2), so the worker provably reaches the contended write.

- **Findings (raised only; author/Board rule):**
  1. **[MAJOR · contract fidelity] `suspend-revoke-delegation-grant.command.ts:51,127-133` — suspend/revoke return `identity_delegation_not_controller`, a code OUTSIDE those contracts' frozen error registers.** Doc-4C §C9 enumerates the suspend register (PassB:595) and revoke register (PassB:621) as EXACTLY `identity_delegation_invalid_input · identity_delegation_forbidden · identity_delegation_not_found · identity_delegation_state_invalid`; `identity_delegation_not_controller` is registered ONLY on `create_delegation_grant` (PassB:582, where the caller targets a vendor PROFILE, not a grant). The register omission reads deliberate: on suspend/revoke the caller probes a grant ID, so a distinguishable "exists but not yours" code is exactly what the §C9 preamble collapse (Finding 2) forecloses. The slice test PINS the nonconforming code (`delegation-grant-slice.test.ts:441-444`), entrenching the drift into the wire face. Disposition proposal (one patch with Finding 2): representative-party caller → `identity_delegation_forbidden` (AUTHORIZATION — the register's only SCOPE-failure mapping); non-party → `identity_delegation_not_found` collapse; update the pinned test + add the two discriminating fixtures.
  2. **[MINOR · non-disclosure] non-party existence disclosure at the app layer.** `findDelegationGrantById` (`delegation-grant.repository.ts:133-161`) loads by bare id with NO party predicate; a third-org caller (any org whose member holds `can_manage_delegations` — every Owner/Director) passing a real grant id reaches the SCOPE check and receives an AUTHORIZATION error distinguishable from NOT_FOUND — an existence oracle over other tenants' delegation relationships. Frozen anchors: Doc-4C §C9 preamble protected-fact rule ("delegation/membership existence beyond a caller's scope is collapsed", PassB:55; Doc-4A §7.5) + Doc-2 §6 hard rule ("service-role queries always filter by organization scope"). App-layer authz is PRIMARY (Doc-6C §6.2a) — the collapse must not depend on the executor's RLS posture (an ENABLE-only policy set does not bind a table-owner/service executor). Latent today (out-of-wire; tests exercise only party callers). Disposition proposal: fold into the Finding-1 patch — party-scope the load (`organization_id IN (controlling, representative)` predicate or post-load party check → NOT_FOUND for non-parties) + a third-org discriminating test asserting the same NOT_FOUND outcome as an absent id.
  3. **[MINOR · D7 conformance test gap] atomicity direction 2 ("no audit row without a successful write") is unpinned.** The REFERENCE checklist (§4.10) demands the conformance suite prove "conflict→no-write/**no-audit**"; the slice suite proves direction 1 (injected append failure → rollback, no grant row) but NO failure-path test asserts ZERO audit rows: the illegal-edge matrix (test:540-568) asserts status-unchanged only; stale-token (test:466-483), not_controller (test:430-448) and the create guard tests assert no-write only. A regression that appends the audit BEFORE the guard/CAS (or outside the outcome check) would ship phantom rows into the immutable ledger undetected. Disposition proposal: assert `auditFor(g.id)` empty on each lifecycle failure path + an audit-count delta of 0 across the create-failure block; test-only.
  4. **[MINOR · test gap] the default-`valid_to` POLICY branch is entirely unexercised though injectable.** `create-delegation-grant.command.ts:92-112` (`durationToMs`) + `:206-211` run only when `validTo` is omitted; every test supplies `validTo: FUTURE`, so the POLICY read, the duration interpreter (four unit arms + the integer-seconds arm + the throw-on-unparseable guard) and the `validFrom + duration` computation have zero coverage. No W2-IDN-7 seed is needed: `deps.configValueQuery` is injectable — a stub returning `{ value: "365d" }` pins the computed window today (+ one unparseable-value rejection). Disposition proposal: two tests in the same patch checkpoint; test-only. (The runtime dependency itself is adjudicated acceptable — judgment call (c).)
  5. **[NIT] `create-delegation-grant.command.ts:139-146`** — the representative≠controlling distinct-org check is evaluated at SYNTAX as VALIDATION, where the frozen matrix places it at DELEGATION, after AUTHZ (PassB:581). Deny-leg-only, input-derived, no disclosure, in-register code — benign; the wire-face WP should align the stage order when the §B.4 matrix becomes wire-observable.

  - **Membership (§5.2, :480-487):** frozen text = `invited ──accept──▶ pending ──verification complete──▶ active` · `active ──suspend──▶ suspended ──reinstate──▶ active` · `active|suspended ──remove──▶ removed (terminal; audit retained)` · `invited ──expire/revoke──▶ removed` ⇒ exactly **7 edges**; the machine = exactly those 7; `removed` sole terminal ✔; the Doc-4M-collapsed `invited → active` is correctly ABSENT and explicitly pinned false in the suite (test:218). The 5×5 pair-table + terminal no-outgoing are suite-proven.
  - **User (no §5 machine):** Doc-2 §10.2 carries a status enum only; Doc-4M M4 has NO user row, and its classification rules (:105 "A §3 status enum is not a lifecycle state machine.
